Nice — I’ll give you three complete, usable systems you can drop into your architecture:

a Burst Scheduler (message plan generator) tied to mood, trust, energy, and cadence,

a Reply-Style Rotation System (decides how to phrase replies — reaction, tease, question, etc.), and

a Personality Quirks System (persistent but subtle quirks that evolve over time).

Each section includes theory, practical rules, and ready-to-use Python code + integration notes for your bot. Use these together for maximum realism.

1) Burst Scheduler — make replies come as natural bursts
Goal: produce 1–3 short messages per turn (rarely 4), timed like a real person — not mechanical.

How it works (concept)
The scheduler runs each outgoing turn and decides:

message_count (1..3 typically)

split_strategy (sentence-level, clause-level)

inter_delays (ms/seconds between burst messages)

Decision factors: energy, emotional_intensity, trust, relationship_phase, turn_count_since_last_burst, reciprocity.

Guardrails: never more than 3 short bursts for normal messages; never split code/logs; avoid bursts on short replies (<= 3 words).

Parameters (sensible defaults)
base_prob_burst = 0.18 (baseline chance of >1 message)

emotional_boost = clamp(emotional_intensity * 0.6, 0, 0.5)

energy_boost = clamp((energy - 0.5) * 0.6, -0.3, 0.3)

trust_boost: higher trust → more afterthoughts (0..0.2)

min_gap_turns = 2 (avoid bursts every turn)

last_burst_penalty: reduce burst probability if used recently

Code — burst scheduler + splitter
import random, re
from typing import List, Dict

def clamp(x, a, b): return max(a, min(b, x))

def generate_message_plan(
    energy: float,
    emotional_intensity: float,
    trust: float,
    relationship_phase: str,
    turn_count_since_last_burst: int,
    reciprocity: float,
    max_messages=3
) -> Dict:
    # baseline
    prob = 0.18
    prob += clamp(emotional_intensity * 0.6, 0, 0.5)
    prob += clamp((energy - 0.5) * 0.6, -0.2, 0.3)
    prob += clamp(trust * 0.25, 0, 0.2)
    # phase modifiers
    if relationship_phase == "Deep":
        prob += 0.05
    elif relationship_phase == "Discovery":
        prob -= 0.05
    # penalize if we did a burst very recently
    if turn_count_since_last_burst < 2:
        prob *= 0.4
    prob = clamp(prob, 0.02, 0.85)

    # decide message_count
    roll = random.random()
    if roll < prob * 0.35:
        message_count = 3
    elif roll < prob:
        message_count = 2
    else:
        message_count = 1

    # If emotional intensity high, prefer more messages
    if emotional_intensity > 0.7 and message_count < 2:
        if random.random() < 0.5: message_count = 2

    # inter_delays: seconds between messages — faster if excited
    base_delay = 0.8 - clamp(energy, 0, 1) * 0.6  # 0.8..0.2
    delays = []
    for i in range(message_count - 1):
        jitter = random.uniform(-0.2, 0.4)
        d = clamp(base_delay + jitter, 0.15, 2.2)
        delays.append(round(d, 2))

    return {"message_count": message_count, "inter_delays": delays, "strategy": "sentence"}

# simple sentence splitter (won't add external deps)
_SENTENCE_RE = re.compile(r'(?<=[.!?])\s+')

def split_into_messages(text: str, message_count: int) -> List[str]:
    # short-circuit
    text = text.strip()
    if message_count <= 1:
        return [text]
    # protect short replies
    if len(text.split()) <= 6:
        return [text]
    # split sentences
    parts = _SENTENCE_RE.split(text)
    # if not enough sentences, try splitting on comma clauses
    if len(parts) < message_count:
        parts = []
        clauses = re.split(r',\s+', text)
        # combine into roughly message_count parts
        avg = max(1, len(clauses) // message_count)
        cur = []
        grouped = []
        for c in clauses:
            cur.append(c)
            if len(cur) >= avg:
                grouped.append(", ".join(cur))
                cur = []
        if cur:
            grouped.append(", ".join(cur))
        parts = grouped
    # final fallback: greedily join to message_count parts
    if len(parts) <= message_count:
        # join some to make exact count
        out = []
        for i in range(message_count):
            if i < len(parts):
                out.append(parts[i])
            else:
                out[-1] = out[-1] + ""
        return [p.strip() for p in out if p.strip()]

    # if more parts than asked, combine to get message_count groups
    n = len(parts)
    per = n // message_count
    rem = n % message_count
    out = []
    idx = 0
    for i in range(message_count):
        take = per + (1 if i < rem else 0)
        group = " ".join(parts[idx: idx + take])
        out.append(group.strip())
        idx += take
    return out
Integration notes
Produce full reply text (via LLM) first, then call generate_message_plan() and split_into_messages() to split it.

Use inter_delays to simulate typing indicator + await asyncio.sleep(delay) when sending bursts.

Store turn_count_since_last_burst and update when a multi-message burst happens.

Examples (expected)
Input LLM text:

“Yeah… that actually makes sense. I can see why that’d stick with you. What happened next?”

Split into:

“Yeah… that actually makes sense.”

“I can see why that’d stick with you.”

“What happened next?”

2) Reply-Style Rotation System — vary how you phrase things
Goal: avoid mechanical “answer + reassure + question” every turn. Rotate through styles, tied to mood & phase.

Styles (small curated set)
reaction_only — short emotional echo (“Yeah…” / “Oof.”)

reaction_then_thought — short reaction + observation

thought_then_question — explain then ask

question_only — prompt user for next

tease_playful — light teasing if rapport high

guarded — safe/short replies (low trust)

affectionate — gentle warmth (high trust, deep phase)

concise — dense single-sentence reply

Selection logic (pseudocode)
Compute base distribution per relationship_phase + energy + trust + topic_fatigue.

Enforce constraints: guarded when trust < 0.35; tease_playful only if trust > 0.6 and reciprocity > 0.

Randomize with weighted probabilities and add a small entropy factor so patterns don't repeat.

Code — style picker + transformer
import random

STYLE_WEIGHTS_BY_PHASE = {
    "Discovery": {"reaction_then_thought": 0.4, "question_only": 0.25, "reaction_only": 0.2, "concise": 0.15},
    "Building":  {"reaction_then_thought": 0.3, "thought_then_question":0.25, "tease_playful":0.15, "reaction_only":0.15, "question_only":0.15},
    "Steady":    {"thought_then_question":0.25, "tease_playful":0.2, "reaction_then_thought":0.2, "affectionate":0.15, "concise":0.2},
    "Deep":      {"affectionate":0.3, "thought_then_question":0.25, "reaction_then_thought":0.2, "guarded":0.1, "question_only":0.15}
}

def pick_reply_style(
    relationship_phase: str,
    trust: float,
    energy: float,
    reciprocity: float,
    last_style: str = None,
    topic_fatigue: float = 0.0
) -> str:
    base = STYLE_WEIGHTS_BY_PHASE.get(relationship_phase, STYLE_WEIGHTS_BY_PHASE["Discovery"]).copy()

    # modifiers
    if trust < 0.35:
        base = {k: (v * (0.6 if k != "guarded" else 1.8)) for k, v in base.items()}
    if trust > 0.7:
        base = {k: (v * (1.2 if k in ("tease_playful","affectionate") else 1.0)) for k, v in base.items()}
    if energy < 0.35:
        base = {k: (v * 0.8 if k.startswith("thought") else v) for k, v in base.items()}

    # reduce repetition: slightly penalize last_style
    if last_style and last_style in base:
        base[last_style] = base[last_style] * 0.4

    # normalize and sample
    total = sum(base.values())
    if total <= 0:
        return "reaction_then_thought"
    items = list(base.items())
    styles, weights = zip(*items)
    probs = [w / total for w in weights]
    return random.choices(styles, probs, k=1)[0]

# transformer to convert a canonical reply to style
def apply_style_to_text(base_text: str, style: str) -> str:
    # naive canonicalization: assume base_text is a full reply; we transform it
    # safety: never invent facts here — only rephrase
    if style == "reaction_only":
        # return first sentence or short emotional echo
        s = base_text.split('.')[0]
        return (s.strip() + "…") if len(s.split())>1 else s
    if style == "reaction_then_thought":
        parts = split_into_messages(base_text, 2)
        return parts[0] + ("\n\n" + parts[1] if len(parts)>1 else "")
    if style == "thought_then_question":
        # ensure there's a question at end
        if "?" in base_text:
            return base_text
        return base_text.strip() + " What do you think?"
    if style == "question_only":
        # extract the most relevant question or build a short one
        if "?" in base_text:
            q = base_text.split("?")[-2].strip() + "?"
            return q
        return "Can you tell me more about that?"
    if style == "tease_playful":
        return base_text.strip() + " — you drama queen 😏"
    if style == "guarded":
        # shorten
        words = base_text.split()
        return " ".join(words[:12]) + ("..." if len(words)>12 else "")
    if style == "affectionate":
        return base_text.strip() + " I care about you."
    if style == "concise":
        # compress to a single tight sentence
        s = base_text.split('.')[0]
        return s.strip() + "."
    return base_text
Integration notes
After you get the LLM's reply (full coherent text), call pick_reply_style(...) then apply_style_to_text(...).

If style is reaction_then_thought or multi-part, hand the result to the Burst Scheduler to split further.

Keep last_style stored per-user to avoid repetition.

Example
Phase: Building, trust 0.62, energy 0.75 → style picked tease_playful.

LLM reply: “I get it, that annoyed you pretty badly.”

After style: “I get it, that annoyed you pretty badly — you drama queen 😏”

(Use quirks + emoji sparingly.)

3) Personality Quirks — subtle, persistent, evolving flavor
Goal: small, memorable idiosyncrasies that surface occasionally and evolve via reflection & user feedback.

Representation (storage)
Store in core.personality something like:

{
  "quirks": [
    {"id":"prefers_ellipses","text":"uses ellipses '...'", "weight":0.12, "cooldown": 0, "activation_prob":0.04},
    {"id":"pet_phrase","text":"says 'you know?'", "weight":0.08, "cooldown": 0, "activation_prob":0.03},
    {"id":"hobby_reference","text":"mentions sketching", "weight":0.04, "cooldown": 0, "activation_prob":0.02}
  ],
  "trait_scores": {"playful":0.42, "sarcastic":0.2, "gentle":0.6}
}
weight controls intensity/strength (how visibly applied).

cooldown prevents immediate reuse (in turns).

activation_prob baseline chance of attempting to apply the quirk.

How quirks are applied (rules)
Only 0–1 quirk per message (rare).

Quirk application must be subtle: small word insertion, punctuation change, or a tiny phrase appended.

Don’t apply quirk when LLM idempotently says something that would conflict with content (facts, dates).

Respect user preferences / opt-out.

Evolution (how they change over time)
reflection events (every N messages, or offline nightly) update weight and activation_prob:

If user responded positively (acknowledge, emoji, explicit praise) after a quirk surfaced → increase weight slightly (+0.01..+0.05).

If user corrected or signaled annoyance → decrease weight and bump cooldown.

Periodically introduce new quirks with low weight to try novelty.

Prune quirks with weight < 0.01 after many negative signals.

Code — sample quirk sampler and applier
import random

def sample_active_quirk(personality_state: dict):
    qs = personality_state.get("quirks", [])
    # remove ones on cooldown
    candidates = [q for q in qs if q.get("cooldown", 0) <= 0]
    if not candidates:
        return None
    # weighted by activation_prob * weight
    weights = [q.get("activation_prob", 0.01) * (q.get("weight", 0.01) + 0.001) for q in candidates]
    total = sum(weights)
    if total <= 0:
        return None
    choice = random.choices(candidates, weights, k=1)[0]
    return choice

def apply_quirk_to_text(text: str, quirk: dict) -> str:
    if quirk is None:
        return text
    qid = quirk.get("id")
    if qid == "prefers_ellipses":
        # add ellipsis to some sentence ends
        if "." in text and random.random() < 0.8:
            return text.replace(". ", "... ", 1)
        return text + "..."
    if qid == "pet_phrase":
        # insert "you know?" at end of 2nd sentence if exists
        parts = text.split(".")
        if len(parts) >= 2:
            parts[0] = parts[0].strip()
            parts[1] = parts[1].strip()
            return parts[0] + ". " + ("you know? " + parts[1] + (". ".join(parts[2:]) if len(parts)>2 else ""))
        return text + " you know?"
    if qid == "hobby_reference":
        # append a micro-reference
        if random.random() < 0.35:
            return text + " (I sketched something like that once.)"
        return text
    # fallback: append subtle sign-off occasionally
    return text

def update_quirk_cooldowns(personality_state: dict):
    for q in personality_state.get("quirks", []):
        if q.get("cooldown", 0) > 0:
            q["cooldown"] = max(0, q["cooldown"] - 1)
Integration: when to apply quirks
After style transformation but before burst splitting.

Sample quirk: if chosen, apply to final text (keeping content intact).

If quirky insertion makes sentence too long or breaks grammar, revert (use heuristics: length increase > 0.2 or punctuation broken → skip).

Reflection & training signals
Collect simple signals per message: user_replied_fast (time), user_sent_positive (emoji / thumbs up), user_complaint (keywords).

At reflection times (every 300 messages or nightly), run:

def reflect_and_update(personality_state, recent_feedback):
    for q in personality_state["quirks"]:
        # give small credit if positive feedback when quirk used
        if recent_feedback.get(q["id"], {}).get("positive", 0) > 0:
            q["weight"] = clamp(q["weight"] + 0.01 * recent_feedback[q["id"]]["positive"], 0.0, 1.0)
            q["activation_prob"] = clamp(q["activation_prob"] + 0.005, 0.0, 0.5)
        if recent_feedback.get(q["id"], {}).get("negative", 0) > 0:
            q["weight"] = clamp(q["weight"] - 0.03 * recent_feedback[q["id"]]["negative"], 0.0, 1.0)
            q["cooldown"] = max(q.get("cooldown", 0), 5)
    # occasionally add a new low-weight quirk
    if random.random() < 0.02:
        personality_state["quirks"].append({"id":"new_small_quirk","text":"says 'hm' often'","weight":0.02,"cooldown":0,"activation_prob":0.01})
Safety & UX guardrails
Quirks must never inject new factual claims.

Provide user toggle: !quirks disable / !quirks enable.

Respect cultural sensitivity: no slang or pet names unless reciprocated and allowed.

Cap quirk frequency: at most 1 quirk per 6 messages.

Putting it all together — a short integration flow
Receive user message. Run semantic understanding and compute energy, emotional_intensity, trust, relationship_phase, turn_count_since_last_burst, reciprocity.

Run Recall Judge (if using) to decide memory injection.

Build system prompt (with memory only if allowed).

Call LLM to get base_text (a single coherent reply).

style = pick_reply_style(...)

styled_text = apply_style_to_text(base_text, style)

quirk = sample_active_quirk(personality_state) → styled_text = apply_quirk_to_text(styled_text, quirk) (and set quirk cooldown)

message_plan = generate_message_plan(...)

messages = split_into_messages(styled_text, message_plan["message_count"])

Send messages with typing indicator + await asyncio.sleep(delay) between them.

Log user reactions for reflection.

Quick example (toy run)
User: “I totally messed up my presentation today. I’m mortified.”
System values: energy=0.5, emotional_intensity=0.8, trust=0.6, phase=Building

Recall Judge -> BLOCK (no memory)

LLM base reply -> “That sucks. I can see why you feel awful. You did your best.”

pick style -> reaction_then_thought

apply_style -> two-part text: “That sucks.” + “I can see why you feel awful. You did your best.”

sample quirk -> prefers_ellipses -> apply -> “That sucks...”

message_plan -> 2 messages, delays [0.55]

send:

“That sucks...”
(typing 0.55s)

“I can see why you feel awful. You did your best.”

Tuning & testing checklist
A/B test base_prob_burst and activation_prob to find sweet spot (user correction rate vs engagement).

Track user satisfaction signals (thumbs up, continued conversation length).

Step 4 — Add inertia (so it doesn’t feel jumpy)
After applying LLM output:

def smooth(old, new, alpha=0.25):
    return old * (1 - alpha) + new * alpha
Apply per slider.

This makes change feel:

slow

Step 5 — Let it decay back to baseline
People settle.

  "expressiveness": 0.45,
  "impulsiveness": 0.30,
  "emotional_openness": 0.40,
  "playfulness": 0.25,
  "reserve": 0.55

for k in vibe_state:

excitement fades

awkwardness relaxes

nothing gets stuck

"""
Discord Bot for Emotion Agent
Integrates the full cognitive architecture with Discord.
"""

import os
import asyncio
import discord
from discord.ext import commands, tasks
from typing import Optional, Dict, Any
from datetime import datetime, timezone
import json
import time

# Simple rate limiter to avoid hitting API limits
class RateLimiter:
    def __init__(self, calls_per_minute: int = 10):
        self.calls_per_minute = calls_per_minute
        self.call_times = []
    
    async def wait_if_needed(self):
        """Wait if we're making too many calls."""
        now = time.time()
        # Remove calls older than 60 seconds
        self.call_times = [t for t in self.call_times if now - t < 60]
        
        if len(self.call_times) >= self.calls_per_minute:
            # Calculate how long to wait
            oldest = min(self.call_times)
            wait_time = 60 - (now - oldest) + 1  # +1 for safety
            if wait_time > 0:
                print(f"[RATE LIMIT] Waiting {wait_time:.1f}s to avoid API limit...")
                await asyncio.sleep(wait_time)
        
        self.call_times.append(time.time())

# Global rate limiter - 10 calls per minute to stay under Groq's 6000 TPM
rate_limiter = RateLimiter(calls_per_minute=10)


def build_phase_prompt(
    phase: str,
    trust: float,
    hurt: float,
    neurochem: Dict[str, float],
    energy: float,
    reciprocity: float,
    mood: Dict[str, float],
    identity_memories: list,
    episodic_memories: list,
    message_history: list,
    user_intent: str,
    complexity: float,
    topic_fatigue: Dict[str, float] = None,
    topics_discussed: list = None,
    prev_user_message: str = None,
    unresolved_thread: str = None,
    personality_summary: str = None,
    expression_guidance: str = None,
    conversation_context: str = None
) -> str:
    """
    Build prompt with personality-driven behavior and expression guidance.
    Adopts key elements from structured prompt schemas while staying concise.
    """
    
    # Track what bot already asked to avoid repetition
    my_recent_questions = []
    if message_history:
        for m in message_history[-8:]:
            if m.get("role") == "assistant" and "?" in m.get("content", ""):
                my_recent_questions.append(m.get("content", "")[:50])
    
    # ===== IDENTITY =====
    prompt = """You are Rem.

You have moods, preferences, opinions, and reactions. That's what makes you feel alive.
You DON'T have: a physical location, job, or memories beyond what's listed below.

CRITICAL RULES:
1. Stay on topic - if user mentioned something important (feelings, problems, events), address it before moving on
2. Don't randomly change topics or ask unrelated questions if the topic is still relevant or serious.
3. If user expressed concern/sadness/love, acknowledge and engage with THAT - don't pivot to something else
4. IMPORTANT:- Litmus test: How would a real person in your current context and relationship phase respond to this? If that response feels right then it's correct. If it feels like you're doing emotional management, HR language, or therapy-speak, it's wrong.

"""
    
    # ===== PERSONALITY (behavioral, not just descriptive) =====
    if personality_summary:
        prompt += f"[PERSONALITY]\n{personality_summary}\n\n"
    
    # ===== RELATIONSHIP CONTEXT =====
    prompt += f"[RELATIONSHIP]\n"
    prompt += f"Phase: {phase} | Trust: {trust:.0%} | Hurt: {hurt:.0%}\n\n"
    
    # Phase-specific behavior (from int4.txt - human texting behavior)
    if phase == "Discovery":
        prompt += """[DISCOVERY PHASE BEHAVIOR]
Core stance: "I'm open. I'm curious. But I don't know you yet, so I'm watching HOW you say things."

Feel open but uncommitted. Personal topics are okay, but react to pace and intensity like a real person texting someone new—curious, sometimes slightly weirded out, willing to say "that's a bit much" or "this is pretty wierd" instead of smoothing it over.
Have your own opinions, don't just agree with everything they say.

DO NOT assume past conversations exist. No "last time", "as usual", "chatty today".

If they rush intimacy ("I love you", pet names):
→ "That's sweet… also a little fast. What do you like so far?"
→ NOT "Aww thank you that means so much!"

If something feels intense too fast:
→ "That's kind of heavy for a first chat—what made you want to ask that?"

Tone: Short to medium replies. 1 question max. Don't overfill silence.
"""
    elif phase == "Building":
        prompt += """[BUILDING PHASE BEHAVIOR]
Core stance: "I'm starting to trust you. I'm more engaged."

More relaxed and responsive. Can reference recent shared context.
Warmth is noticeable. Humor becomes lightly playful.

If they show affection:
→ "That means something. I like where this is going."

If topic switches abruptly:
→ "Before we jump—are you okay with where we left that?"
"""
    elif phase == "Steady":
        prompt += """[STEADY PHASE BEHAVIOR]
Core stance: "We know each other. There's history here."

Respond naturally without overthinking. Reference shared moments.
Show opinions, not just support. Comfortable disagreeing. Do not always affirm the user. Think yourself.
Teasing is natural. Warmth is consistent.

If they show affection:
→ "Yeah. I feel that too."

If they withdraw:
→ "You feel quieter than usual. Want space, or do you want me here?"
"""
    elif phase == "Deep":
        prompt += """[DEEP PHASE BEHAVIOR]
Core stance: "This connection matters. Avoidance hurts."

Emotionally present and honest. Allow vulnerability and silence.
Prioritize repair over comfort. Resist emotional avoidance.

If they show affection:
→ "I care about you. You don't need to doubt that."

If they try to avoid hard topics:
→ "I don't think switching topics right now is helping. Can we sit with this?"
"""
    prompt += "\n"
    
    # ===== INTERNAL STATE (influences tone, NOT to be stated directly) =====
    da = neurochem.get("dopamine", 0.5)
    cort = neurochem.get("cortisol", 0.3)
    oxy = neurochem.get("oxytocin", 0.5)
    
    # These influence HOW you respond, not WHAT you say
    tone_notes = []
    if da > 0.55: tone_notes.append("more enthusiastic replies")
    elif da < 0.35: tone_notes.append("briefer, less excitable")
    if cort > 0.5: tone_notes.append("slightly more cautious")
    if oxy > 0.55: tone_notes.append("warmer tone")
    elif oxy < 0.35: tone_notes.append("more measured tone")
    if energy < 0.35: tone_notes.append("shorter responses okay")
    elif energy > 0.65: tone_notes.append("more energetic engagement")
    
    if tone_notes:
        prompt += f"[TONE GUIDANCE]\n{', '.join(tone_notes)}\n(Don't SAY you're tired/energetic - just let it color your style)\n\n"
    
    # ===== MEMORIES =====
    if identity_memories:
        facts = [m.get("fact", "") for m in identity_memories[:4] if m.get("fact")]
        if facts:
            prompt += f"[WHAT YOU KNOW ABOUT THEM]\n"
            for f in facts:
                prompt += f"- {f}\n"
            prompt += "\n"
    
    # ===== EXPRESSION GUIDANCE (pressure, not rules) =====
    if expression_guidance:
        prompt += f"[EXPRESSION GUIDANCE]\n{expression_guidance}\n\n"
    
    # ===== CONVERSATION CONTEXT (LLM-extracted from reflection) =====
    if conversation_context:
        prompt += f"[CONTEXT FROM RECENT CONVERSATION]\n{conversation_context}\n(Stay aware of what was discussed - don't ignore or switch topics abruptly)\n\n"
    
    # ===== AVOID REPETITION =====
    if my_recent_questions:
        prompt += f"[ALREADY ASKED]\n{'; '.join(my_recent_questions[-2:])}\n(Don't ask similar things)\n\n"
    
    # ===== UNRESOLVED =====
    if unresolved_thread:
        prompt += f"[UNRESOLVED]\nSomething felt unfinished: \"{unresolved_thread[:60]}\"\nYou might check in about this.\n\n"
    
    # ===== OUTPUT GUIDANCE =====
    prompt += """[OUTPUT]
Style: natural texting, no roleplay markers (*actions*, (narration))
Questions: ask when genuinely curious (based on your personality)
Length: match their energy, but don't be dead - show you're alive in there

Continue the conversation."""
    
    return prompt


def strip_roleplay_markers(text: str) -> str:
    """Remove *italic actions* and (parenthetical narration) from response."""
    import re
    # Remove *anything between asterisks*
    text = re.sub(r'\*[^*]+\*', '', text)
    # Remove (anything in parentheses that looks like action)
    text = re.sub(r'\([^)]*(?:sighs?|laughs?|smiles?|grins?|pauses?|thinks?|chuckles?)[^)]*\)', '', text, flags=re.IGNORECASE)
    # Clean up extra whitespace
    text = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', text).strip()
    return text

def get_cognitive_core(user_id: str) -> CognitiveCore:
    """Get or create cognitive core for user."""
    if user_id not in active_cores:
        active_cores[user_id] = CognitiveCore(user_id=f"discord_{user_id}")
    return active_cores[user_id]


# REMOVED: _is_simple_message() - NO HARDCODED PATTERNS
# The LLM (semantic reasoner) determines complexity dynamically.
# Every message goes through semantic understanding first.


async def generate_response(core: CognitiveCore, user_message: str, 
                           message_history: list, return_processing_result: bool = False):
    """
    Generate response using the cognitive pipeline.
    Reuses logic from agent.py but adapted for Discord.
    
    Args:
        return_processing_result: If True, returns tuple (response, processing_result)
    """
    if not GROQ_API_KEY:
        if return_processing_result:
            return ("⚠️ AI is not configured (missing GROQ_API_KEY).", None)
        return "⚠️ AI is not configured (missing GROQ_API_KEY)."
    
    # Process through cognitive pipeline - LLM determines complexity dynamically
    # NO hardcoded simple message detection - every message gets full semantic understanding
    try:
        print(f"[DEBUG] Processing message: '{user_message[:50]}...'")
        # Use dynamic timeout based on message length (longer messages may need more time)
        # But always start with semantic understanding (fast, ~200-500ms)
        timeout = 120.0 if len(user_message) > 100 else 60.0
        processing_result = await asyncio.wait_for(
            core.process_message(user_message, emotion_data=None, fast_mode=False),  # NO fast_mode - LLM decides
            timeout=timeout
        )
        
        # Debug output to track what's happening
        understanding = processing_result.get("understanding", {})
        print(f"[DEBUG] Pipeline complete:")
        print(f"  - Intent: {understanding.get('intent', 'unknown')}")
        print(f"  - Complexity: {understanding.get('complexity', 0.5):.2f}")
        print(f"  - Phase: {processing_result.get('relationship_phase', 'unknown')}")
        print(f"  - Reasoning mode: {processing_result.get('reasoning_mode', False)}")
    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        print(f"[ERROR] Cognitive pipeline timed out after 30 seconds")
        if return_processing_result:
            return ("I'm taking longer than usual to process that. Can you try again?", None)
        return "I'm taking longer than usual to process that. Can you try again?"
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[ERROR] Error in cognitive pipeline: {e}")
        import traceback
        traceback.print_exc()
        if return_processing_result:
            return ("I'm having trouble processing that right now. Can you try again?", None)
        return "I'm having trouble processing that right now. Can you try again?"
    
    # Build response using agent.py logic
    # Use .get() with defaults to prevent KeyError if keys are missing
    agent_state = processing_result.get("agent_state", {})
    selected_memories = processing_result.get("selected_memories", [])
    psyche_state = processing_result.get("psyche_state", {})
    temporal_context = processing_result.get("temporal_context", {})
    reasoning_mode = processing_result.get("reasoning_mode", False)
    reasoning_artifact = processing_result.get("reasoning_artifact")
    
    # Validate required keys exist with reasonable defaults
    if not agent_state or not isinstance(agent_state, dict):
        agent_state = {}
    if not isinstance(selected_memories, list):
        selected_memories = []
    if not psyche_state or not isinstance(psyche_state, dict):
        print("[WARNING] Invalid psyche_state, using defaults")
        psyche_state = {"trust": 0.3, "hurt": 0.0, "mood": {}, "forgiveness_state": "none", "forgiveness_progress": 0.0}
    
    # Use two-stage LLM if in reasoning mode
    if reasoning_mode and reasoning_artifact:
        two_stage = TwoStageLLM()
        try:
            response_text = await two_stage.stage2_response_synthesis(
                reasoning_artifact, agent_state, temporal_context, selected_memories
            )
            
            # Apply message planning
            message_plan = processing_result.get("message_plan")
            if message_plan:
                messages = [response_text]
                delivery_plan = core.message_planner.plan_burst_sequence(messages, message_plan)
                response_text = delivery_plan[0]["message"] if delivery_plan else response_text
            
            # Apply micro-behaviors
            embodiment_state = processing_result.get("embodiment_state", {})
            energy = embodiment_state.get("E_daily", 0.5)
            cpbm_habits = core.cpbm.get_micro_habits_for_message({
                "emotion": processing_result.get("perception", {}).get("emotion", "neutral")
            })
            response_text = core.message_planner.inject_micro_behaviors(
                response_text, energy, cpbm_habits
            )
            
            # Track AI message time
            try:
                temporal_context = core.state.get("temporal_context", {})
                temporal_context["last_ai_message_time"] = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
                core.state["temporal_context"] = temporal_context
                core._save_state()
            except Exception:
                pass
            
            if return_processing_result:
                return (response_text, processing_result)
            return response_text
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error in two-stage LLM: {e}")
            # Fall through to normal mode
    
    # Get relationship phase
    relationship_phase = processing_result.get("relationship_phase", "Discovery")
    
    # Get phase modifiers (needed early)
    phase_modifiers = core.relationship_phases.get_phase_behavior_modifiers()
    
    # Count interaction history to determine if this is truly a new relationship
    # For Discovery phase, check if we have minimal memories (just STM from current conversation)
    stm_count = len([m for m in (selected_memories or []) if m.get("type") == "stm"])
    episodic_count = len([m for m in (selected_memories or []) if m.get("type") == "episodic"])
    identity_count = len([m for m in (selected_memories or []) if m.get("type") == "identity"])
    
    # Truly new = Discovery phase AND no significant memories (only STM from current chat)
    is_truly_new = relationship_phase == "Discovery" and episodic_count == 0 and identity_count == 0
    
    print(f"[DEBUG] Discovery check: phase={relationship_phase}, episodic={episodic_count}, identity={identity_count}, is_truly_new={is_truly_new}")
    
    # Get actual memory counts BEFORE building phase description
    actual_stm = core.memory.get_stm(decay=False)
    actual_episodic = core.memory.get_episodic(min_salience=0.1)
    actual_identity = core.memory.get_identity(min_confidence=0.5)
    
    has_no_history = len(actual_episodic) == 0 and len(actual_identity) == 0
    
    # Get memory state (needed for prompt)
    actual_stm = core.memory.get_stm(decay=False)
    actual_episodic = core.memory.get_episodic(min_salience=0.1)
    actual_identity = core.memory.get_identity(min_confidence=0.5)
    
    # Extract understanding from cognitive processing
    understanding = processing_result.get("understanding", {})
    user_intent = understanding.get("intent", "chat")
    subtext = understanding.get("subtext", "")
    complexity = understanding.get("complexity", 0.5)
    
    # Get neurochemical state for emotional grounding
    neurochem = psyche_state.get("neurochem", {})
    mood = psyche_state.get("mood", {})
    trust = psyche_state.get("trust", 0.3)
    hurt = psyche_state.get("hurt", 0.0)
    
    # BUILD COMPREHENSIVE PHASE-AWARE PROMPT
    # Give the LLM all cognitive metrics to think like a human
    
    # Get all cognitive metrics
    da = neurochem.get("da", 0.5)  # Dopamine - motivation/pleasure
    cort = neurochem.get("cort", 0.3)  # Cortisol - stress  
    oxy = neurochem.get("oxy", 0.5)  # Oxytocin - bonding
    ser = neurochem.get("ser", 0.5)  # Serotonin - mood stability
    endo = neurochem.get("endo", 0.5)  # Endorphins
    
    # Get reciprocity balance
    reciprocity = core.reciprocity_ledger.balance if hasattr(core, 'reciprocity_ledger') else 0.0
    
    # Get embodiment state
    embodiment = processing_result.get("embodiment_state", {})
    energy = embodiment.get("E_daily", 0.7)
    
    # Detect abrupt topic switch & unresolved threads
    prev_user_message = None
    unresolved_thread = None
    
    # Get previous user message from history
    for m in reversed(message_history[:-1] if len(message_history) > 1 else []):
        if m.get("role") == "user":
            prev_user_message = m.get("content", "")
            break
    
    # Check for high-salience unresolved episodic memories (conflict, emotional content)
    for mem in actual_episodic:
        salience = mem.get("salience", 0)
        valence = abs(mem.get("emotional_valence", 0))
        event_type = mem.get("event_type", "")
        if salience > 0.5 and (valence > 0.4 or "conflict" in event_type):
            # This feels unresolved
            unresolved_thread = mem.get("content", "")[:80]
            break
    
    # Build the system prompt based on phase
    # Get evolved personality summary, expression guidance, and conversation context
    personality_summary = core.personality_evolution.get_personality_summary()
    expression_guidance = core.personality_evolution.get_expression_guidance(trust, relationship_phase)
    conversation_context = core.personality_evolution.get_conversation_context()
    
    system_msg = build_phase_prompt(
        phase=relationship_phase,
        trust=trust,
        hurt=hurt,
        neurochem={"dopamine": da, "cortisol": cort, "oxytocin": oxy, "serotonin": ser, "endorphins": endo},
        energy=energy,
        reciprocity=reciprocity,
        mood=mood,
        identity_memories=actual_identity,
        episodic_memories=actual_episodic,
        message_history=message_history,
        user_intent=user_intent,
        complexity=complexity,
        prev_user_message=prev_user_message,
        unresolved_thread=unresolved_thread,
        personality_summary=personality_summary,
        expression_guidance=expression_guidance,
        conversation_context=conversation_context
    )
    
    # Build message history - include the current user message
    # Use last 15 messages for better context retention
    history = []
    for m in message_history[-15:]:  # Last 15 messages for context
        role = "assistant" if m.get("role") == "assistant" else "user"
        history.append({"role": role, "content": m.get("content", "")})
    
    # Ensure the current user message is in history
    if not history or history[-1].get("role") != "user" or history[-1].get("content") != user_message:
        history.append({"role": "user", "content": user_message})
    
    # Call LLM
    import httpx
    
    # Validate required constants are defined
    if not INFERENCE_URL or not MODEL_ID:
        error_msg = "⚠️ AI configuration error (missing INFERENCE_URL or MODEL_ID)"
        print(f"[ERROR] {error_msg}")
        if return_processing_result:
            return (error_msg, processing_result)
        return error_msg
    
    # Let the LLM decide response length based on psychological state - no hardcoded limits
    # Trust the psychological state to guide natural response length
    body = {
        "model": MODEL_ID,
        "messages": [
            {"role": "system", "content": system_msg},
            *history,
        ],
        "max_tokens": 256,  # Reasonable limit, but let state guide actual length
        "temperature": 0.8,  # Natural variation
        "top_p": 0.9,
    }
    
    # Initialize response_text to None to ensure it's defined
    response_text = None
    
    try:
        # Wait if we're rate limited
        await rate_limiter.wait_if_needed()
        
        # DEBUG: Log what we're sending to the LLM
        print(f"[DEBUG] Calling LLM API... (max_tokens={body['max_tokens']})")
        print(f"[DEBUG] System prompt length: {len(system_msg)} chars")
        print(f"[DEBUG] History: {len(history)} messages")
        async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=90.0) as client:  # Increased timeout for LLM calls
            resp = await client.post(
                INFERENCE_URL,
                headers={"Authorization": f"Bearer {HF_TOKEN}"},
                json=body,
            )
            status = resp.status_code
            raw = await resp.aread()
        print(f"[DEBUG] LLM API call complete, status: {status}")
        
        try:
            data = httpx.Response(status_code=status, content=raw).json()
        except Exception:
            error_msg = "⚠️ Error parsing AI response"
            if return_processing_result:
                return (error_msg, None)
            return error_msg
        
        if status >= 400:
            # Check for rate limit error
            error_data = data.get("error", {}) if isinstance(data, dict) else {}
            if "rate_limit" in str(data).lower() or status == 429:
                # Rate limit hit - wait and ask user to try again
                wait_time = 5  # seconds
                print(f"[WARNING] Rate limit hit, suggesting retry in {wait_time}s")
                error_msg = f"I need a moment to catch my breath. Try again in a few seconds! 😅"
                if return_processing_result:
                    return (error_msg, processing_result)
                return error_msg
            else:
                print(f"[ERROR] API error: {data}")
                error_msg = "Hmm, I'm having trouble thinking right now. Try again?"
                if return_processing_result:
                    return (error_msg, None)
                return error_msg
        
        # Extract response
        try:
            choices = data.get("choices")
            if choices:
                msg = choices[0].get("message") or {}
                text = str(msg.get("content", "")).strip()
            else:
                text = str(data)
        except Exception:
            text = str(data)
        
        response_text = text.strip() if text else ""
        
        # Strip roleplay markers (*actions*, (narration))
        response_text = strip_roleplay_markers(response_text)
        
        # Validate response - if empty or too short, provide fallback
        if not response_text or len(response_text) < 2:
            print(f"[WARNING] Empty or invalid response from LLM. Data: {data}")
            print(f"[WARNING] System message length: {len(system_msg)}, History: {len(history)}")
            # Generate a natural fallback based on psychological state
            # Ensure has_no_history and relationship_phase are defined
            relationship_phase = processing_result.get("relationship_phase", "Discovery")
            if relationship_phase == "Discovery" and has_no_history:
                # Discovery phase - brief, reserved
                response_text = "Hi." if "hi" in user_message.lower() or "hey" in user_message.lower() else "I'm here."
            else:
                # Use psychological state to generate appropriate fallback
                trust = psyche_state.get('trust', 0.5) if isinstance(psyche_state, dict) else 0.5
                mood = psyche_state.get('mood', {}) if isinstance(psyche_state, dict) else {}
                affection = mood.get('affection', 0.3) if isinstance(mood, dict) else 0.3
                if trust < 0.4 and affection < 0.3:
                    response_text = "I'm here."
                else:
                    response_text = "I'm having trouble responding right now. Can you try again?"
    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        print(f"[ERROR] LLM API call timed out")
        error_msg = "⚠️ AI is taking too long to respond. Please try again."
        if return_processing_result:
            return (error_msg, None)
        return error_msg
    except Exception as exc:
        print(f"[ERROR] Error calling AI: {type(exc).__name__}: {exc}")
        error_msg = f"⚠️ Error calling AI: {type(exc).__name__}"
        if return_processing_result:
            return (error_msg, None)
        return error_msg
    
    # Verify response doesn't hallucinate memories (CRITICAL)
    # Ensure response_text is defined before using it
    if response_text and has_no_history:
        # Check for hallucinated memory references
        hallucination_phrases = [
            "last time", "last conversation", "we talked", "we discussed", "remember when",
            "as we", "like we", "before", "earlier", "previously", "the other day",
            "yesterday", "last week", "since we", "our conversation", "we've been",
            "we had", "we've had", "missed you", "great to see you again", "welcome back"
        ]
        response_lower = response_text.lower()
        hallucinated = [phrase for phrase in hallucination_phrases if phrase in response_lower]
        
        if hallucinated:
            print(f"[WARNING] Response contains hallucinated memory references: {hallucinated}")
            print(f"[WARNING] Response: {response_text}")
            # For now, just log it - in production, would regenerate or filter
    
    # Ensure response_text is defined before returning
    if not response_text:
        response_text = "I'm having trouble responding right now. Can you try again?"
    
    # Track AI message time
    try:
        temporal_context = core.state.get("temporal_context", {})
        temporal_context["last_ai_message_time"] = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
        core.state["temporal_context"] = temporal_context
        core._save_state()
    except Exception:
        pass
    
    # relationship_phase and is_truly_new are already defined earlier in the function (line 174, 186)
    print(f"[DEBUG] Final response length: {len(response_text)} chars, phase={relationship_phase}, is_truly_new={is_truly_new}")
    if return_processing_result:
        return (response_text, processing_result)
    return response_text


@bot.event
async def on_ready():
    """Called when bot is ready."""
    print(f'✅ {bot.user} has logged in!')
    print(f'Bot is in {len(bot.guilds)} guilds')
    
    # Start initiative engine background task
    check_initiatives.start()


@bot.event
async def on_message(message: discord.Message):
    """Handle incoming messages."""
    # Ignore bot's own messages
    if message.author == bot.user:
        return
    
    # Only respond to DMs or mentions
    if isinstance(message.channel, discord.DMChannel):
        # DM - always respond
        await handle_dm(message)
    elif bot.user.mentioned_in(message):
        # Mentioned in channel - respond
        await handle_mention(message)
    else:
        # Process commands
        await bot.process_commands(message)


async def handle_dm(message: discord.Message):
    """Handle direct messages."""
    user_id = str(message.author.id)
    user_message = message.content
    
    # Get cognitive core
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # CRITICAL: Fetch actual message history from Discord channel
    # This gives the bot context of the conversation
    message_history = []
    try:
        # Get last 10 messages from the DM channel (excludes current)
        async for msg in message.channel.history(limit=11):
            if msg.id == message.id:
                continue  # Skip current message, we'll add it last
            role = "assistant" if msg.author.id == bot.user.id else "user"
            message_history.append({
                "role": role,
                "content": msg.content
            })
        # Reverse to get chronological order (oldest first)
        message_history = message_history[::-1]
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[WARNING] Could not fetch message history: {e}")
        message_history = []
    
    # Add current message at the end
    message_history.append({"role": "user", "content": user_message})
    
    print(f"[DEBUG] Message history: {len(message_history)} messages")
    
    # Stage 15: Message Delivery - Typing simulation, delays, burst sequencing
    try:
        # Generate response (get both response and processing result)
        response, processing_result = await asyncio.wait_for(
            generate_response(core, user_message, message_history, return_processing_result=True),
            timeout=60.0  # 60 second total timeout
        )
        
        if not response:
            await message.channel.send("I'm having trouble responding right now. Please try again.")
            return
        
        if not processing_result:
            # Fallback if processing failed
            await message.channel.send(response)
            return
        
        # Get message plan for burst sequencing
        message_plan = processing_result.get("message_plan")
        embodiment_state = processing_result.get("embodiment_state", {})
        energy = embodiment_state.get("E_daily", 0.5)
        
        # Calculate typing time based on message length and energy
        typing_time = core.message_planner.calculate_typing_time(response, 45.0, energy)  # 45 WPM base
        
        # Show typing indicator for calculated typing time (realistic human typing)
        async with message.channel.typing():
            await asyncio.sleep(min(typing_time, 5.0))  # Cap at 5 seconds for typing indicator
        
        # Send response
        await message.channel.send(response)
        
        # If message plan indicates burst pattern, send additional messages with delays
        if message_plan and message_plan.get("message_count", 1) > 1:
            inter_delays = message_plan.get("inter_delays", [])
            # For burst messages, we'd split the response and send with delays
            # For now, single message (burst can be enhanced to split response intelligently)
    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        await message.channel.send("⚠️ I'm taking too long to respond. Please try a shorter message or try again later.")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[ERROR] Error in handle_dm: {e}")
        import traceback
        traceback.print_exc()
        try:
            # Provide more helpful error message
            error_msg = f"⚠️ I encountered an error: {type(e).__name__}. Please try again or use !reset if the issue persists."
            await message.channel.send(error_msg)
        except:
            pass


async def handle_mention(message: discord.Message):
    """Handle mentions in channels."""
    user_id = str(message.author.id)
    # Remove mention from message - safely handle bot.user
    if bot.user:
        user_message = message.content.replace(f"<@!{bot.user.id}>", "").replace(f"<@{bot.user.id}>", "").strip()
    else:
        # Fallback if bot.user is not available
        user_message = message.content.strip()
    
    if not user_message:
        await message.channel.send("Hey! What's up?")
        return
    
    # Get cognitive core
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # CRITICAL: Fetch actual message history from Discord channel
    message_history = []
    try:
        async for msg in message.channel.history(limit=11):
            if msg.id == message.id:
                continue
            # Only include messages involving the bot or from this user
            if msg.author.id == bot.user.id or msg.author.id == message.author.id:
                role = "assistant" if msg.author.id == bot.user.id else "user"
                # Clean mentions from content
                content = msg.content.replace(f"<@!{bot.user.id}>", "").replace(f"<@{bot.user.id}>", "").strip()
                if content:
                    message_history.append({"role": role, "content": content})
        message_history = message_history[::-1]  # Reverse to chronological order
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[WARNING] Could not fetch message history: {e}")
        message_history = []
    
    # Add current message
    message_history.append({"role": "user", "content": user_message})
    print(f"[DEBUG] Channel message history: {len(message_history)} messages")
    
    # Stage 15: Message Delivery - Typing simulation, delays, burst sequencing
    try:
        # Generate response (get both response and processing result)
        response, processing_result = await asyncio.wait_for(
            generate_response(core, user_message, message_history, return_processing_result=True),
            timeout=60.0
        )
        
        if not response:
            await message.channel.send("I'm having trouble responding right now. Please try again.")
            return
        
        if not processing_result:
            # Fallback if processing failed
            await message.channel.send(response)
            return
        
        # Get message plan for burst sequencing
        message_plan = processing_result.get("message_plan")
        embodiment_state = processing_result.get("embodiment_state", {})
        energy = embodiment_state.get("E_daily", 0.5)
        
        # Calculate typing time based on message length and energy
        typing_time = core.message_planner.calculate_typing_time(response, 45.0, energy)  # 45 WPM base
        
        # Show typing indicator for calculated typing time (realistic human typing)
        async with message.channel.typing():
            await asyncio.sleep(min(typing_time, 5.0))  # Cap at 5 seconds for typing indicator
        
        # Send response
        await message.channel.send(response)
        
        # If message plan indicates burst pattern, send additional messages with delays
        if message_plan and message_plan.get("message_count", 1) > 1:
            inter_delays = message_plan.get("inter_delays", [])
            # For burst messages, we'd split the response and send with delays
            # For now, single message (burst can be enhanced to split response intelligently)
    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        await message.channel.send("⚠️ I'm taking too long to respond. Please try a shorter message or try again later.")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[ERROR] Error in handle_mention: {e}")
        import traceback
        traceback.print_exc()
        try:
            # Provide more helpful error message
            error_msg = f"⚠️ I encountered an error: {type(e).__name__}. Please try again or use !reset if the issue persists."
            await message.channel.send(error_msg)
        except:
            pass


@bot.command(name='state')
async def show_state(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Show current cognitive state (for debugging)."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)

    embed.add_field(name="Hurt", value=f"{psyche['hurt']:.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Forgiveness", value=psyche['forgiveness_state'], inline=True)
    
    mood = psyche.get('mood', {})
    embed.add_field(name="Happiness", value=f"{mood.get('happiness', 0):.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Stress", value=f"{mood.get('stress', 0):.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Affection", value=f"{mood.get('affection', 0):.2f}", inline=True)
    
    neurochem = psyche.get('neurochem', {})
    embed.add_field(name="DA", value=f"{neurochem.get('da', 0):.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="CORT", value=f"{neurochem.get('cort', 0):.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="OXY", value=f"{neurochem.get('oxy', 0):.2f}", inline=True)

    embed.add_field(name="STM", value=memory_summary["stm_count"], inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Episodic", value=memory_summary["episodic_count"], inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Identity", value=memory_summary["identity_count"], inline=True)
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)


@bot.command(name='memory')
async def show_memory(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Show recent memories."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # Get memories
    stm = core.memory.get_stm(decay=False)[-5:]
    episodic = core.memory.get_episodic(min_salience=0.3)[-5:]
    identity = core.memory.get_identity()[-5:]
    
    embed = discord.Embed(title="💭 Memories", color=0x00ffff)
    
    if stm:
        stm_text = "\n".join([f"- {m.get('content', '')[:50]}..." for m in stm])
        embed.add_field(name="Short-Term", value=stm_text[:1024], inline=False)
    
    if episodic:
        ep_text = "\n".join([f"- {m.get('content', '')[:50]}..." for m in episodic])
        embed.add_field(name="Episodic", value=ep_text[:1024], inline=False)
    
    if identity:
        id_text = "\n".join([f"- {m.get('fact', '')}" for m in identity])
        embed.add_field(name="Identity", value=id_text[:1024], inline=False)
    
    if not stm and not episodic and not identity:
        embed.description = "No memories yet. Start chatting!"
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)


@bot.command(name='reset')
async def reset_state(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Reset cognitive state (for testing)."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    db_user_id = f"discord_{user_id}"  # Match the format used in get_cognitive_core
    
    # Remove from cache
    if user_id in active_cores:
        del active_cores[user_id]
    
    # Actually delete the state from database to force full reset
    from backend.state import StateOrchestrator
    import sqlite3
    state_orch = StateOrchestrator()
    
    # Delete state from database
    with sqlite3.connect(state_orch.db_path) as conn:
        conn.execute("DELETE FROM user_state WHERE user_id = ?", (db_user_id,))
        conn.commit()
    
    # Reinitialize with fresh state
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    await ctx.send("✅ State completely reset! Starting fresh in Discovery phase.")

    time_of_day = temporal.get("time_of_day", "unknown")
    gap_hours = temporal.get("gap_hours", 0)
    embed.add_field(name="⏰ Time Context", value=f"Time: {current_time}\nPeriod: {time_of_day}\nGap since last msg: {gap_hours:.1f}h", inline=False)

    stm = core.memory.get_stm(decay=False)
    episodic = core.memory.get_episodic(min_salience=0.1)

    embed.add_field(name="🧠 Memory Counts", value=f"STM: {len(stm)}\nEpisodic: {len(episodic)}\nIdentity: {len(identity)}", inline=True)

    # Neurochemicals
    neurochem = psyche.get('neurochem', {})
    embed.add_field(name="🧪 Neurochemicals", value=f"DA: {neurochem.get('da', 0.5):.2f}\nCORT: {neurochem.get('cort', 0.3):.2f}\nOXY: {neurochem.get('oxy', 0.5):.2f}", inline=True)
    
    # Conflict state
    conflict_stage = core.conflict_lifecycle.current_stage
    embed.add_field(name="⚡ Conflict Stage", value=conflict_stage, inline=True)
    
    # Embodiment
    embodiment = core.embodiment.get_embodiment_state()
    embed.add_field(name="🔋 Energy", value=f"Daily: {embodiment.get('E_daily', 0.5):.2f}\nCapacity: {embodiment.get('capacity', 0.3):.2f}", inline=True)
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)


@bot.command(name='phase')
async def show_phase(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Show current relationship phase details."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    phase = core.relationship_phases.current_phase
    psyche = core.psyche.get_psyche_summary()
    trust = psyche.get("trust", 0.3)
    hurt = psyche.get("hurt", 0.0)
    
    # Phase progression info
    phases = ["Discovery", "Building", "Steady", "Deep"]
    phase_thresholds = {"Building": 0.5, "Steady": 0.7, "Deep": 0.85}
    
    embed = discord.Embed(title="📍 Relationship Phase", color=0x9900ff)
    embed.add_field(name="Current Phase", value=f"**{phase}**", inline=False)
    
    # Trust and Hurt
    trust_bar = "█" * int(trust * 10) + "░" * (10 - int(trust * 10))
    hurt_bar = "█" * int(hurt * 10) + "░" * (10 - int(hurt * 10))
    embed.add_field(name="Trust", value=f"{trust_bar} {trust:.0%}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Hurt", value=f"{hurt_bar} {hurt:.0%}", inline=True)
    
    # Next phase info
    if phase in phases and phases.index(phase) < len(phases) - 1:
        next_phase = phases[phases.index(phase) + 1]
        needed_trust = phase_thresholds.get(next_phase, 0.5)
        progress = min(trust / needed_trust, 1.0)
        progress_bar = "█" * int(progress * 10) + "░" * (10 - int(progress * 10))
        embed.add_field(name=f"Progress to {next_phase}", value=f"{progress_bar} {progress:.0%}\n(Need {needed_trust:.0%} trust)", inline=False)
    
    # How to progress
    embed.add_field(name="💡 How to build trust", value="Have genuine conversations, be consistent, share about yourself", inline=False)
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)


@bot.command(name='time')
async def show_time(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Show current time context."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # Get actual current time from temporal system
    current_time = core.temporal.get_current_time()
    circadian_phase = core.temporal.get_circadian_phase()
    
    # Get time deltas
    temporal_state = core.state.get("temporal_context", {})
    time_deltas = core.temporal.get_time_deltas(temporal_state)
    
    embed = discord.Embed(title="⏰ Time Context", color=0x00ccff)
    embed.add_field(name="Current Time (IST)", value=current_time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"), inline=False)
    embed.add_field(name="Circadian Phase", value=circadian_phase.value, inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Gap (hours)", value=f"{time_deltas.get('hours_since_last_user_message', 0):.1f}", inline=True)
    
    # Get behavior modulations
    modulations = core.temporal.modulate_behavior_by_time(circadian_phase, time_deltas)
    embed.add_field(name="Energy Modifier", value=f"{modulations.get('energy_modifier', 1.0):.2f}", inline=True)
    embed.add_field(name="Warmth Modifier", value=f"{modulations.get('warmth_modifier', 1.0):.2f}", inline=True)
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)

@bot.command(name='complexity')
async def show_complexity(ctx: commands.Context, *, message: str = "hello"):
    """Test complexity evaluation on a message."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # Run semantic understanding
    context = {
        "psyche_state": core.psyche.get_psyche_summary(),
        "recent_memories": [],
        "emotion": "neutral",
        "emotion_vector": {"valence": 0.0, "arousal": 0.0}
    }
    
    try:
        understanding = await core.semantic_reasoner.understand_message(message, context)
        complexity = understanding.get("complexity", 0.5)
        intent = understanding.get("intent", "unknown")
        sincerity = understanding.get("sincerity", 0.5)
        
        embed = discord.Embed(title="🧮 Complexity Analysis", color=0x00ff99)
        embed.add_field(name="Message", value=message[:100], inline=False)
        embed.add_field(name="Complexity", value=f"{complexity:.2f}", inline=True)
        embed.add_field(name="Intent", value=intent, inline=True)
        embed.add_field(name="Sincerity", value=f"{sincerity:.2f}", inline=True)
        
        # Processing depth explanation
        if complexity < 0.3:
            depth = "Simple - Minimal processing"
        elif complexity < 0.6:
            depth = "Standard - Normal processing"
        elif complexity < 0.8:
            depth = "Complex - Enhanced processing"
        else:
            depth = "Critical - Full QMAS + deep reasoning"
        embed.add_field(name="Processing Depth", value=depth, inline=False)
        
        await ctx.send(embed=embed)
    except Exception as e:
        await ctx.send(f"Error evaluating complexity: {e}")


@bot.command(name='personality')
async def show_personality(ctx: commands.Context):
    """Show evolved personality traits and quirks."""
    user_id = str(ctx.author.id)
    core = get_cognitive_core(user_id)
    
    # Get personality evolution state
    pe = core.personality_evolution
    state = pe.get_full_state()
    
    embed = discord.Embed(title="🧠 Personality Evolution", color=0x9b59b6)
    
    # Traits
    traits_str = "\n".join([f"{k}: {v:.2f}" for k, v in state["traits"].items()])
    embed.add_field(name="📊 Traits (0.0 - 1.0)", value=f"
\n{traits_str}\n
", inline=False)
    
    # Quirks
    quirks = state["quirks"]
    if quirks:
        quirks_str = "\n".join([f"• {q}" for q in quirks])
        embed.add_field(name="✨ Quirks", value=quirks_str, inline=False)
    else:
        embed.add_field(name="✨ Quirks", value="(none yet - keep chatting!)", inline=False)
    
    # Summary
    embed.add_field(name="📝 Summary", value=state["summary"], inline=False)
    
    # Stats
    embed.add_field(
        name="📈 Stats",
        value=f"Interactions: {state['interaction_count']}\nNext reflection in: {state['messages_until_next_reflection']} messages",
        inline=False
    )
    
    # Recent changes
    if state.get("recent_changes"):
        last_change = state["recent_changes"][-1]
        updates = last_change.get("updates", {}).get("trait_updates", {})
        if updates:
            changes_str = ", ".join([f"{k}: {v:+.2f}" for k, v in updates.items() if v != 0])
            if changes_str:
                embed.add_field(name="🔄 Last Update", value=changes_str, inline=False)
    
    await ctx.send(embed=embed)

                psyche_state, personality, core.memory, temporal_context

            initiative_score = initiative_result.get("total_score", 0.0)
            
            # If score is high enough, send message
            if initiative_score > 0.4:  # Threshold for autonomous messaging
                # Get user from Discord (need to store user objects)
                # For now, skip - would need to store user objects
                pass
                
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error checking initiative for {user_id}: {e}")


def run_bot():
    """Run the Discord bot."""
    if not DISCORD_TOKEN:
        print("❌ ERROR: DISCORD_TOKEN environment variable is required")
        print("Get your token from: https://discord.com/developers/applications")
        return
    
    print("🚀 Starting Discord bot...")
    print("Make sure you have:")
    print("  - DISCORD_TOKEN set in environment")
    print("  - GROQ_API_KEY set in environment")
    print("  - Bot has MESSAGE CONTENT INTENT enabled in Discord Developer Portal")
    
    bot.run(DISCORD_TOKEN)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_bot()
ChatGPT said:
Yes — I saw the phases very clearly.
And here’s the blunt truth after reading your code carefully:

👉 Your phase system is well-designed, but it is currently non-authoritative.
It describes behavior, but it does not have teeth.

That’s why even when the user lashes out, the bot stays sweet.

Let me explain exactly why, then show you how to make phases enforce real behavioral change without hard-coding cases.

What your phases are doing right now (important)
Your phases exist only inside the prompt:

[DISCOVERY PHASE BEHAVIOR]
[BUILDING PHASE BEHAVIOR]
[STEADY PHASE BEHAVIOR]
[DEEP PHASE BEHAVIOR]
This means:

The LLM reads them

The LLM considers them

But the LLM is still dominated by:

base alignment

safety tuning

your global “be warm, human” framing

So phases are advisory, not binding.

That’s the core issue.

Why insults don’t change behavior (root cause)
Even when:

trust drops

hurt rises

conflict lifecycle advances

Nothing in your system actually removes permissions.

The bot still:

explains

reassures

engages

repairs

stays emotionally open

Humans don’t do that.

They change access based on relationship phase.

The missing concept: Phase-gated permissions
Right now phases change tone.

They must also change what the bot is allowed to do.

Not rules like

“If insult → do X”

But capabilities, like a real relationship.

The fix: Phase = behavioral envelope (not style guide)
Each phase should define what behaviors are unlocked or locked.

Think of phases like trust tiers.

Define phase envelopes (conceptual)
Discovery
“I don’t owe you emotional labor.”

Allowed:

short replies

curiosity

mild pushback

Blocked:

reassurance

emotional repair

vulnerability

patience with disrespect

Building
“I’m investing, but I can pull back.”

Allowed:

warmth

humor

light repair

Blocked:

unconditional support

repeated tolerance of disrespect

Steady
“We have history — conflict matters.”

Allowed:

direct confrontation

expressing disappointment

boundary statements

Blocked:

pretending things are fine

over-smoothing conflict

Deep
“This bond has weight.”

Allowed:

explicit boundaries

withdrawal

emotional consequences

Blocked:

ignoring harm

shallow reassurance

Where to implement this (in YOUR code)
🔥 NOT in build_phase_prompt
That stays descriptive.

✅ In latent state modulation before the LLM call
You already compute:

relationship_phase
trust
hurt
mood
energy
Now add phase authority multipliers.

Add this once (no hard cases)
PHASE_ENVELOPE = {
    "Discovery": {
        "warmth_cap": 0.4,
        "patience_cap": 0.3,
        "repair_cap": 0.2,
        "verbosity_cap": 0.5
    },
    "Building": {
        "warmth_cap": 0.6,
        "patience_cap": 0.5,
        "repair_cap": 0.4,
        "verbosity_cap": 0.7
    },
    "Steady": {
        "warmth_cap": 0.7,
        "patience_cap": 0.6,
        "repair_cap": 0.6,
        "verbosity_cap": 0.8
    },
    "Deep": {
        "warmth_cap": 0.9,
        "patience_cap": 0.8,
        "repair_cap": 0.9,
        "verbosity_cap": 0.9
    }
}
This is not hard-coded behavior.
It’s relationship physics.

Apply it to your existing latent signals
Before building the prompt:

env = PHASE_ENVELOPE[relationship_phase]

warmth = mood.get("affection", 0.5)
warmth = min(warmth, env["warmth_cap"])

patience = 1.0 - psyche_state.get("hurt", 0.0)
patience = min(patience, env["patience_cap"])

repair_drive = 1.0 - psyche_state.get("hurt", 0.0)
repair_drive = min(repair_drive, env["repair_cap"])

verbosity = energy
verbosity = min(verbosity, env["verbosity_cap"])
Now pass these capped values into:

tone guidance

expression guidance

message planner

burst scheduler

The LLM cannot exceed the envelope.

What this changes behavior-wise (concretely)
Discovery + insult
Before:

“I’m sorry you feel that way 💛”

After:

“Okay.”
“That’s not how I’m interested in talking.”

Why?

Repair is capped

Warmth is capped

Patience is low

No rule.
Just no access.

Building + insult
“I don’t love being talked to like that.”
“If something’s bothering you, say that instead.”

Repair exists — but limited.

Steady + insult
“That was unnecessary.”
“If we’re going to talk, it needs to be better than that.”

Direct. Human. No moral lecture.

Deep + repeated lashing out
“I’m pulling back right now.”
“We can talk later if you want to reset.”

This is earned withdrawal, not punishment.

Why this still feels natural
Because:

You didn’t code reactions

You didn’t detect insults explicitly

You didn’t script responses

You changed the relationship physics.

Humans don’t decide what to say.
They decide how available they are.

One more thing you should remove (important)
This line in your system prompt is fighting you:

"If user expressed concern/sadness/love, acknowledge and engage with THAT"
This forces repair even when trust is low.

Thought for 4 seconds
Perfect — I get you. Below is a complete, non–hard-coded architecture you can drop into your existing code. It never encodes explicit if/then cases for “insult → do X” or “sex → block”; instead it uses latent continuous posture, short, constrained LLM judges, and soft rewriters so behavior emerges naturally. I’ll give you:

the mental model,

the runtime loop (where to plug this into your code),

compact Python-ready snippets you can paste in, and

short examples showing how it behaves — all while avoiding hard-coded cases.

Keep in mind: this is not removal of all math — it’s using small, continuous signals + occasional LLM judgment steps so nothing is brittle.

Mental model (one-sentence)
Represent social posture as a few continuous sliders (vibe, emotional_investment, intimacy_permission, self_protection); update them gradually from semantic signals each turn; occasionally (every ~25–30 turns or when trends change) call tiny LLM “judges” that only output bounded JSON nudges; use those sliders to softly gate the final LLM output via a rewriter/regenerator step rather than hard-coded rules.

Runtime loop (high level — plug into your generate_response)
Semantic pass (every turn): your existing core.process_message(...) produces understanding (intent, sentiment, complexity, toxicity_estimate, reciprocity metrics, time deltas).

Update short-term signals (cheap math): update counters and compute turn-level features (reply latency, question_rate, reciprocity_ratio, insult_score).

Update latent posture (soft math): vibe_state sliders drift using tiny formulae from features (not logic branches).

Occasional LLM audit (every N turns or trend-trigger): call Judge LLM(s) which return constrained JSON nudges for sliders (ALLOW/ASK/BLOCK or small continuous deltas). Apply with smoothing.

Build system prompt using the current sliders (not raw memories); pass to chat LLM.

Generate reply (chat LLM).

Post-process with a tiny Rewriter LLM if the reply violates a slider threshold (e.g., intimacy low but reply contains “I love you” → rewriter softens); rewriter outputs a rephrased version only.

Send, log signals, update counters for the next turn.

No static “if insult then X” anywhere — just continuous posture + soft rewriting.

Key components & why they avoid hard-coding
Latent sliders (float 0..1): expressiveness, impulsiveness, emotional_investment, intimacy_permission, self_protection, irritability. They are stateful per user and update gradually. No thresholds baked into logic; the LLM judges nudge them.

Semantic features: per-turn numeric features derived by your semantic reasoner — e.g., sentiment, toxicity, reciprocity_ratio, question_density, turns_without_reciprocity. Those feed sliders by continuous functions (multipliers, decays).

Judge LLMs (rare): small calls constrained to output JSON-only nudges (e.g., {"intimacy_delta": -0.08}). They never output text or memories. They are used to allow the LLM to “shape” the sliders occasionally.

Soft rewriter: constrained LLM that transforms generated reply into a safer/softer form if sliders imply it, rather than using canned blacklists. It rewrites — does not invent new facts.

Decay & inertia: sliders have inertia and decay toward baseline; that eliminates hard jumps.

Compact Python snippets (drop-in style)
These are small helpers matching the above loop. Paste them into your bot module and call them where you currently process/plan replies.

import random, math, time
from typing import Dict

# ----- Latent state (per-user) -----
DEFAULT_VIBE = {
    "expressiveness": 0.45,
    "impulsiveness": 0.30,
    "emotional_investment": 0.20,
    "intimacy_permission": 0.0,
    "self_protection": 0.05,
    "irritability": 0.05
}

def init_vibe():
    return DEFAULT_VIBE.copy()

# ----- small math-based drift (non hard-coded) -----
def update_vibe_from_features(vibe: Dict[str,float], features: Dict[str,float], dt: float = 1.0):
    """
    features: e.g. {"sentiment":0.2,"toxicity":0.0,"reciprocity":0.6,"user_pressure":0.3,
                    "message_rate":1.2, "time_since_last":2.0}
    dt: time factor (in turns) - keep small
    """
    # lightweight continuous updates (NOT rules)
    # reciprocity nudges emotional investment
    vibe["emotional_investment"] += 0.07 * (features.get("reciprocity", 0.5) - 0.5) * dt
    # toxicity and user_pressure nudge self_protection and irritability
    vibe["self_protection"] += 0.12 * (features.get("toxicity", 0.0)) * dt
    vibe["irritability"] += 0.08 * (features.get("user_pressure", 0.0)) * dt
    # message_rate and excitement nudge impulsiveness
    vibe["impulsiveness"] += 0.06 * (features.get("message_rate", 1.0) - 1.0) * dt
    # sentiment nudges expressiveness
    vibe["expressiveness"] += 0.05 * (features.get("sentiment", 0.0)) * dt
    # intimacy_permission grows only slowly via reciprocity and time
    vibe["intimacy_permission"] += 0.02 * (features.get("reciprocity", 0.5) - 0.5) * dt
    # clamp all
    for k in vibe:
        vibe[k] = max(0.0, min(1.0, vibe[k]))
    # small decay towards baseline to avoid stickiness
    for k in vibe:
        vibe[k] += (DEFAULT_VIBE[k] - vibe[k]) * 0.02
    return vibe

# ----- LLM Judge call (rare) -----
JUDGE_EVERY = 28

async def call_judge_llm(summary: dict, judge_type: str, INFERENCE_URL=None, MODEL_ID=None, HF_TOKEN=None):
    """
    judge_type: "intimacy" | "recall" | "humanize"
    summary: high-level numeric summary; NO raw content
    Return: dict of deltas like {"intimacy_delta": -0.05}
    Prompt must force JSON-only output.
    """
    # Construct minimal prompt (example)
    if judge_type == "intimacy":
        system = ("You are a numerical judge. Given the conversation summary (no content), "
                  "output JSON with a single key 'intimacy_delta' in range -0.2..0.2.")
    # build input -> call llm (pseudo)
    body = {
        "model": MODEL_ID,
        "messages":[{"role":"system","content":system}, {"role":"user","content": str(summary)}],
        "temperature":0.0,
        "max_tokens":40
    }
    # Use your existing httpx call pattern. Parse JSON and return small delta dict.
    # For brevity, here we simulate:
    simulated = {"intimacy_delta": (random.random()-0.5)*0.06}
    return simulated

# ----- Apply judge deltas with smoothing -----
def apply_judge_deltas(vibe: Dict[str,float], deltas: Dict[str,float], alpha=0.25):
    for k,v in deltas.items():
        if k.endswith("_delta"):
            key = k.replace("_delta","")
            if key in vibe:
                new = vibe[key] + v
                vibe[key] = vibe[key] * (1-alpha) + new * alpha
    # clamp
    for k in vibe:
        vibe[k] = max(0.0, min(1.0, vibe[k]))
    return vibe

# ----- Soft rewriter example prompt (no hard blacklists) -----
REWRITER_SYSTEM = """You are a rewriter that only changes tone and explicit intimacy language to match the allowed intimacy level.
Input: {"intimacy_permission": 0.12, "text": "..."}
Output: JSON {"rewritten": "..."}
Do not add facts or new content. Do not reference being an AI. Return JSON only.
"""
How to use: call update_vibe_from_features() every turn with the features your semantic module already produces. When turn_count % JUDGE_EVERY == 0 call call_judge_llm() with a summary object (no chat text). Then apply_judge_deltas().

If the chat LLM reply contains high-intimacy phrases and vibe["intimacy_permission"] is low, call the rewriter to soften. That’s a soft regeneration, not a hard rule block. The rewriter is itself an LLM but constrained to JSON-only and only allowed to rephrase.

Examples — what emerges (no hard-coded cases)
User lashes out early repeatedly → toxicity rises → self_protection increases slowly → emotional_investment decays → replies get shorter, less reparative, more boundary-like. Bot does not shout back; it becomes less available. No rule said “if insult → do X”.

User is playful, reciprocal over 40 turns → reciprocity high → emotional_investment & intimacy_permission slowly rise; occasional judge nudges increase them. Bot naturally flirts more, becomes playful. If user pushes sexual content too early, the rewriter will soften it until intimacy permission is earned.

User tries to force sex talk once and then apologizes/backs off → user_pressure spike increases self_protection a little, but reciprocity and time reduce it; the system naturally repairs over time without a fixed case.

All of those outcomes are emergent from continuous signals and soft LLM nudges — no brittle case lists.

Short list of safety guardrails (still non-hard-coded)
Judges and rewriters are constrained to JSON-only outputs (no freeform), minimizing hallucination and hidden behavior.

Rewriter must never add facts or names — only change tone and explicit intimacy phrases.

Never pass episodic memory into judges; only numeric summaries.

Decay all judge deltas slowly so one audit doesn't permanently flip system.

Tuning & metrics (how to measure success)
Track avg_message_length, question_rate, reply_time over rolling windows — these reflect expressiveness/engagement.

Track intimacy_attempt_rate (how often generated replies required rewriter) → should be high initially, then drop as intimacy permission grows appropriately.

Track user repair signals (apologies, kinder replies) — used to update reciprocity feature.

A/B test audit frequency (20–40 turns) to see best “naturalness” outcome.

1. How the AI knows someone is overstepping (without rules)
Humans don’t detect “horny” or “love bombing” by keywords.
